<div id="review_1941489756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1941489756" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40275186-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494083045p2/40275186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1941489756?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/40275186-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40275186-sarah?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40275186-sarah?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1941489756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17570822953447031537">I'm giving this four stars because in comparison to many other historical fiction books, it certainly deserves that many stars at least. In comparison to Follett's other Kingsbridge novels, sadly, I'd only give it three stars.<br/><br/>There is something magical about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5043.The_Pillars_of_the_Earth__Kingsbridge___1_' title='The Pillars of the Earth (Kingsbridge, #1) by Ken Follett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Pillars of the Earth</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5064.World_Without_End__Kingsbridge___2_' title='World Without End (Kingsbridge, #2) by Ken Follett' rel='nofollow noopener'>World Without End</a>. In those novels Follett weaves together the lives of ordinary people and makes what might otherwise seem mundane, engrossing. They tell the tales of good vs. evil, the many obstacles on the pat</span>
  <span id="freeText17570822953447031537" style="display:none">I'm giving this four stars because in comparison to many other historical fiction books, it certainly deserves that many stars at least. In comparison to Follett's other Kingsbridge novels, sadly, I'd only give it three stars.<br /><br />There is something magical about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5043.The_Pillars_of_the_Earth__Kingsbridge___1_" title="The Pillars of the Earth (Kingsbridge, #1) by Ken Follett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pillars of the Earth</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5064.World_Without_End__Kingsbridge___2_" title="World Without End (Kingsbridge, #2) by Ken Follett" rel="nofollow noopener">World Without End</a>. In those novels Follett weaves together the lives of ordinary people and makes what might otherwise seem mundane, engrossing. They tell the tales of good vs. evil, the many obstacles on the path to righteousness, the triumphs of either side, and the eventual justice received by all. I love these books. They are the kind of books that stay with you over time and beg to be reread.<br /><br />A Column of Fire, unfortunately, just doesn't live up to the enormous standard set by the previous two books. The primary problem is that this is not the tale of that triumphant fictional town of Kingsbridge. This is a novel that spans many settings, languages and countries. It takes a look at the beginning of religious freedom in Europe. It did not have the tight-knit feel of small town drama. The enemies were still evil, but they were vast and many and always seemed so distant.<br /><br />In past books, I was always glued to the page knowing the characters were often going head to head, watching one plan come together and seeing the other characters unravel it piece by piece. There was scheming here, but it often felt impersonal. It happened on a much grander scale and somehow didn't hold my attention as tightly as the smaller, more personal battles of Kingsbridge.<br /><br />However, there are other things to love about this novel. Sylvie is a strong female character that you can't help but root for. I think her character arc was the strongest and perhaps the most interesting. Whenever the plot switched to her viewpoint, I was thrilled to see what she would do next. She competes with the men on a level reminiscent of Aliena in The Pillars of the Earth. I also loved Ned Willard's storyline. Minor <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[: He becomes one of the leaders of a massive network of Protestant spies throughout England and France. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> His story was told well and didn't cross lines of implausibility (which I think might have been an easy trap to fall into given the historical setting).<br /><br />The historical accuracy, to my knowledge, was fantastic and well told. We see the opulent wealth of the Catholic church and French monarchy and aristocracy, religious persecution, naval battles, plays, and traveling acrobatic troupes, and bearbaiting. Follett's portrayal of Queen Elizabeth was fascinating and has me yearning to learn more about her as a historical figure rather than a (semi) fictional character.<br /><br />I would recommend this to anyone who reads historical fiction and is interested in the 16th century. However, if you have read the previous Kingsbridge novels, I would advise that you do not go into this expecting a third. It's fine as it is on its own, but to liken it with its predecessors will bring, in my opinion, disappointment.<br /><br />Thank you to Edelweiss and Viking for providing an eARC to review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17570822953447031537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2121041532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121041532" />
    <a title="Clif Hostetler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/793473-clif-hostetler"><img alt="Clif Hostetler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593302055p2/793473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2121041532?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clif Hostetler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clif Hostetler" href="/user/show/793473-clif-hostetler">Clif Hostetler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781509838370" href="/book/show/35659572-a-column-of-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/793473-clif-hostetler?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2121041532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3220872338131971780">The Reformation was a time when religion was front and center in national, social and personal identity. It was so important that it was common practice to kill those who held incorrect beliefs. The concept of tolerance was generally an abhorrent thought because it suggested that correct religious belief wasn't absolutely important and true. This book is a historical novel about a time when toleration of religious diversity was beginning to take hold during the reign of Queen Elizabeth I. But tr</span>
  <span id="freeText3220872338131971780" style="display:none">The Reformation was a time when religion was front and center in national, social and personal identity. It was so important that it was common practice to kill those who held incorrect beliefs. The concept of tolerance was generally an abhorrent thought because it suggested that correct religious belief wasn't absolutely important and true. This book is a historical novel about a time when toleration of religious diversity was beginning to take hold during the reign of Queen Elizabeth I. But true toleration was still a ways off in the future. In my opinion it was not a good time to be alive.<br /><br />The story moves through 50 eventful years of Reformation history beginning in 1558 during the reign of Bloody Mary of England and finally ending with the Gunpowder Plot of 1605. An epilogue carries the story forward to 1620. History has provided Follett with some spectacular dramatic moments during these years, and he takes full advantage by recreating them with a historian’s eye for detail and a novelist’s gift for narrative suspense. Follett makes sure his fictional characters are present at and playing key roles in all the significant historical events of the second half of the sixteenth century. <br /><br />Among the more dramatic interludes are the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Bartholomew%27s_Day_massacre" rel="nofollow noopener">St. Bartholomew’s Day Massacre</a>, in which Parisian Catholics murdered thousands of Huguenots (French Protestants); the execution of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary, Queen of Scots</a>, an act that sent shock waves throughout Europe; and the miraculous defeat of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Armada" rel="nofollow noopener">Spanish Armada</a> by a much smaller force.<br /><br />Some other lesser know historical events described in this book include the following listed items (not complete):<br />1. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" rel="nofollow noopener">Spanish Inquisition</a> and its secular use to end business completion<br />2. Marriage of Mary Stuart (aka Queen of Scots) to Francis, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis_II_of_France" rel="nofollow noopener">Francis, Dauphin of France</a>, and the official witnessing of its consummation<br />3. The accidental death of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" rel="nofollow noopener">Henry II of France</a><br />4. The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massacre_of_Wassy" rel="nofollow noopener">Massacre of Wassy</a><br />5. The assassination of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis,_Duke_of_Guise" rel="nofollow noopener">Francis, Duke of Guise</a><br />6. Riot in Antwerp that stopped the burning at the stake of a 14 year old girl who refused to recant from being Protestant. (not sure this is historical)<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />I found this event which is similar, but wrong city:<br />On March 28, 1558, five Anabaptists escaped death at the stake, in Rotterdam, Netherlands. (See Martyrs' Mirror, p. 575.) Their names were: Jan Hendriksz, Peter van Eynoven, Evert Nouts, Annetgen Antheunisdochter, and Stijntgen Jansdochter. The executioner had just begun the process of strangling Jan Hendricsz, but he made such slow progress that the spectators became agitated and restless. The crowd soon overpowered the executioner and took control ot the situation. All five prisoners were set tree, so that no one was executed in Rotterdam that day. Three days later, however, one of the liberators, Guert Vllillemszoon, was captured and given the death sentence.<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />7. Mary Queen of Scots escape from Scottish imprisonment and fleeing to England (and eventual doom)<br />8. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regnans_in_Excelsis" rel="nofollow noopener">Papal bull</a> issued by Pope Pius V declaring Queen Elizabeth to be a heretic and releasing all her subjects from any allegiance to her<br />9. The assassination of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_I,_Duke_of_Guise" rel="nofollow noopener">Henry I, Duke of Guise</a><br /><br />Any readers who are prejudice in favor of Catholicism will not find much comfort in these pages. Most of the villains in this story are Catholic. The Puritans represent the extreme of the Protestant side, but within this time period they were not politically powerful. <br /><br />Follett uses the tools of popular fiction to great effect, illuminating a nation’s gradual progress toward modernity. The central theme of the book is the ongoing conflict between tolerance and fanaticism. In Follett’s hands, that story becomes a fascinating narrative.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3220872338131971780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2337089272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2337089272" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2337089272?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2337089272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2766052013442449101"><b>*** 4 ***</b><br/><br/>Ken Follett is not the best writer. What Ken Follett is, is a good observer of the human condition and a very good historical researcher. If you love history and particularly the 16th Century Western European politics and religious wars, this series, and particularly this book is a very good addition to the usual historical fiction variety. For the fans of the Kingsbridge series, this book comes back to the town with the big Cathedral and some familial descendants to the first Tom Build</span>
  <span id="freeText2766052013442449101" style="display:none"><b>*** 4 ***</b><br /><br />Ken Follett is not the best writer. What Ken Follett is, is a good observer of the human condition and a very good historical researcher. If you love history and particularly the 16th Century Western European politics and religious wars, this series, and particularly this book is a very good addition to the usual historical fiction variety. For the fans of the Kingsbridge series, this book comes back to the town with the big Cathedral and some familial descendants to the first Tom Builder from the middle ages. It is sad to see how the changes in laws and rulers affected the Cathedral and the population of the town at large. This volume covers the time of the tumultuous rain of Queen Elizabeth and the battle of the Catholic and Protestant religions for the souls of the citizens of the West. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"... "In the eyes of the church, the Bible was the most dangerous of all banned books—especially translated into French or English, with marginal notes explaining how certain passages proved the correctness of Protestant teaching. Priests said that ordinary people were unable to rightly interpret God’s word, and needed guidance. Protestants said the Bible opened men’s eyes to the errors of the priesthood. Both sides saw reading the Bible as the central issue of the religious conflict that had swept Europe.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />It is brutal. As in the years preceding every change of religion throughout the historical timeline, the established philosophies and the ones challenging them go through a dance of give and take, of debate and bloodshed, and of obsession and disillusionment. Mr. Follett brings the reality of the time in a very realistic and relatable manner, although he puts us more in the observer's role, thus letting us have the emotional separation needed to be able to get through a hefty and merciless read like this one. The history has never been a bone of contention with me, nor is the way he is able to show so many sides of the conflict and numerous ways people perceived and dealt with them. It is the writing. I still have an problem with the way he is able to cover such breath of complex issues, while he is more than shallow when it comes to characters and their interactions. As readers we are affected by the horrors of the reality, but we are not truly allowed to be involved with any of the characters, be them "good" or "bad" guys. We react to the actions, but the characters are a bit flat, the villains being supper evil and the good guys being mostly good and with clear and justifiable motives. Not that there is anything wrong with that, but I really believe that a bit of a personal touch to their characters while interacting would go a very long way and be worthy of the scope of the work he already does so well. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"... “We hanged him in front of Kingsbridge Cathedral. It is the usual place for executions. After all, if you can’t kill a man in front of God’s face you probably shouldn’t kill him at all.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Ned Willard is the main protagonist and a protestant who works for the Queen. We see a span of at least 50 years through his eyes and I have to say, I enjoyed him, but I was not "in love" with him. Honestly, as much as I feel separated from him, he is still the one I could understand and cheer for most out of all the male characters up to now in the series. Out of Margery and Sylvie I preferred Sylvie, the Paris Huguenot, but I understood Margery as well. Overall, I was engrossed in the story from beginning to end and am glad I got to read it. For those who love Follett, he delivers exactly what we have come to expect from him. If you want to read this book, but have not read the previous ones, I think it is completely fine to be read as a standalone. It is full of religion, politics and action, so it does have a lot to offer. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"... “Perhaps we’ve done enough.” Sylvie was shocked. Her mother had never talked this way. Isabelle noticed her reaction and said defensively: “Even God rested on the seventh day, after he made the world.” “Our work isn’t finished.” “Perhaps it never will be, until the Last Trump.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find what you Need in the pages of a Good Book!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2766052013442449101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2305391778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305391778" />
    <a title="ChopinFC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc"><img alt="ChopinFC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545283749p2/51633786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305391778?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=follett">follett</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305391778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12491605542606643736"><b><i>A Column of Fire</i> caps off a perfect ending to an immaculate and masterful series. </b><br/><br/><br/><u>The Kingsbridge series has been nothing but a masterpiece in storytelling, and historical enlightenment! </u> In this latest entry, Follett focus his attention in diverging European religious and political ideology in a devilish entertaining way. At the height of European transition from medieval period into 16th century ‘modern’ time, we see some of the most tumultuous conflicts between Catholics and Protestants. Foll</span>
  <span id="freeText12491605542606643736" style="display:none"><b><i>A Column of Fire</i> caps off a perfect ending to an immaculate and masterful series. </b><br><br><br><u>The Kingsbridge series has been nothing but a masterpiece in storytelling, and historical enlightenment! </u> In this latest entry, Follett focus his attention in diverging European religious and political ideology in a devilish entertaining way. At the height of European transition from medieval period into 16th century ‘modern’ time, we see some of the most tumultuous conflicts between Catholics and Protestants. Follett explores this religious tension to the maximum, with a story that is laced with unforgettable characters and exceeding moments of love and conflict while maintaining historical accuracy. <br><br><br><i>“When a man is certain that he knows God’s will, and is resolved to do it regardless of the cost, he is the most dangerous person in the world.” <br>― Ken Follett, A Column of Fire</i><br><br><br>Follett covers a widely unstable time in European politics after 1558, all seen through the eyes two lovers Ned Willard and Margery Fitzgerald. During that time, the throne of England inherited by the more progressive Elizabeth of Tudor, who unlike her older predecessor sister Mary Tudor, did not believe of burning ‘heretics’ for prescribing to a certain faith. Unlike Mary, Queen Elizabeth believed in religious tolerance and acceptance, despite being a Protestant herself. <br><br><br><br><i>“Might there come a time when people of different faiths did not kill one another?” <br>― Ken Follett, A Column of Fire</i><br> <br><br><b>At the heart of <i>A Column of Fire</i>, lies the tale of two lovers Ned Willard and Margery Fitzgerald. </b> Follett is brilliant at telling historical events through vivid and unique characters- making the story that much more appealing! The main protagonist ‘Ned’ is a balanced Protestant, and becomes one of the main advisors for Queen Elizabeth. Yet his love interest, ‘Margaret’ is a stout Catholic, thus setting up a constant dissonance and tension between both lovers, despite their passion for one another. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1564496763i/27911807.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Ned Willard and Margery Fitzgerald</b><br><br><br><b>Follett narrates the events of the religious time so perfectly! He takes the reader on a whirlwind of historical events, but writes it in such a captivating and engaging manner, that I was left speechless in some moments of the book! </b>The breadth of information and meticulous details are a testament to his historical acumen and preparation for this series. From the Bartholomew Day massacre to Mary Queen of Scotts execution, the Spanish Armada and the Gunpowder plot as well as the personal fortunes of a huge cast of characters, both real and imagined. The results are quite astounding, especially as Follett is able to organically blend it all together in the end! <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564496763ra/27911808.gif" width="400" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>English fleet vs Spanish Armada </b><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Ultimately Follett dazzles the reader with his God-given talent as a storyteller.</u>
</b> I know I’ve praised him plenty in previous books ( Pillars, Eye of Needle, etc.),but his narrative ability to is so engaging, and that is reflective throughout multiple moments in <i>A Column of Fire</i>. <br>Follett has the uncanny ability to convert a topic that is generally dull and rather thick into something magical, and indescribably entertaining. The ability to infuse passion, tension and emotion into historical events is quite demonstrative of his skills as a writer. <br><br><br><br><b><i>Kingbridge Series</i> is his Follett’s magnum opus, with ‘Pillars of the Earth at the helm. This latest entry blew me away with the breadth of historical accuracy, and written in a such a persuasive and entertaining manner that left me speechless at times! My favorite historical fiction series of all times :)<br><br><br>5 Stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12491605542606643736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2274274746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17957823-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597778686p2/17957823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2274274746?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/17957823-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17957823-erin?shelf=library-borrowed">library-borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17957823-erin?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2274274746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12964108630616414182"><i> Yes, I have done this many times:watched a man die knowing that I, more than anyone else, had brought him to his just but dreadful punishment. I did it for my country, which is dear to me; for my sovereign, whom I serve; and for something else, a principle, the belief that a person had the right to make up his own mind about God. <br/> He was the last of many men I sent to hell, but he made me think of the first...</i><br/><br/>Well, my hats off to Mr. Ken Follett on another fantastic historical fiction that I go</span>
  <span id="freeText12964108630616414182" style="display:none"><i> Yes, I have done this many times:watched a man die knowing that I, more than anyone else, had brought him to his just but dreadful punishment. I did it for my country, which is dear to me; for my sovereign, whom I serve; and for something else, a principle, the belief that a person had the right to make up his own mind about God. <br /> He was the last of many men I sent to hell, but he made me think of the first...</i><br /><br />Well, my hats off to Mr. Ken Follett on another fantastic historical fiction that I gorged myself on this quiet Sunday night. When I heard that Follet was giving his fans a third follow up in the series that began with "The Pillars of the Earth" and continued with "World Without End," I must admit that I wondered what else there was to say about the splendid but angsty Kingsbridge. As I come up for air after 900 pages, I will say that it was definitely a treat to revisit the old stomping grounds.But I found myself nostalgic for the craziness of the medieval period and the building of the cathedral. <br /><br />Spanning 1558-1620, Follett, like he did with his 20th century trilogy, blossoms outside the boundaries of England and unfolds the tale of European powers and their religious civil wars that waged between Catholics and Protestants. Like the first two installments, there is political intrigue, young lovers thwarted, villains and heroes, and just down right cruel members of the clergy. But I missed my beloved cathedral that just didn't get enough of the limelight. <br /><br />Although a more extensive character list would have been much appreciated, I do acknowledge that the back of the book has a list of the real historical persons that travel the pages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12964108630616414182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2153882978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2153882978" />
    <a title="Meg - A Bookish Affair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1132408-meg---a-bookish-affair"><img alt="Meg - A Bookish Affair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312494581p2/1132408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2153882978?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meg - A Bookish Affair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meg - A Bookish Affair" href="/user/show/1132408-meg---a-bookish-affair">Meg - A Bookish Affair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132408-meg---a-bookish-affair?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132408-meg---a-bookish-affair?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132408-meg---a-bookish-affair?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153882978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9349611506686536501">4.5 stars. "A Column of Fire" is the third book in Ken Follett's Kingsbridge series. I have not read the first two books but after reading this one, I really want to go back to read those two books as well as some of Follett's other books! That being said, this book works rather well as a standalone book. Standing at over 900 pages, you are in Follett's very capable hands so the pages fly by! This is a historical fiction epic.<br/><br/>The book takes place during a tumultuous time in England's history: th</span>
  <span id="freeText9349611506686536501" style="display:none">4.5 stars. "A Column of Fire" is the third book in Ken Follett's Kingsbridge series. I have not read the first two books but after reading this one, I really want to go back to read those two books as well as some of Follett's other books! That being said, this book works rather well as a standalone book. Standing at over 900 pages, you are in Follett's very capable hands so the pages fly by! This is a historical fiction epic.<br /><br />The book takes place during a tumultuous time in England's history: the late 1500s and early 1600s. The country is going through a major identity crisis as to whether it is a Catholic or a Protestant country. Should everyone be in the same mold or can they have more freedom? Who is the rightful ruler of the country? Who can that ruler trust?<br /><br />This was a time period that was familiar to me but what I appreciated is that for the most part, Follett's characters are just on the edge of history. We meet rulers through them like Queen Elizabeth and Mary, Queen of Scots. We see how calculated each move must be for even these edge-of-history characters in order to be on the "right" side at the "right" time. <br /><br />This book is action packed and kept me on my toes. In some ways, it reminds me of a soap opera. There's a huge cast but each character has their own unique story. Large casts can often be an issue for me because of the likelihood of characters blending together but Follett really does a good job of creating different storylines that intertwine in surprising ways.<br /><br />This was a great read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9349611506686536501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2121940856" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121940856" />
    <a title="Tanja Berg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5935491-tanja-berg"><img alt="Tanja Berg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558953813p2/5935491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2121940856?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanja Berg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanja Berg" href="/user/show/5935491-tanja-berg">Tanja Berg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5935491-tanja-berg?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2121940856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3121589870084689767">I expect sumptuous historical novels from Ken Follett and he definitely delivered again. The cast of villains and heroes is vast. This time the setting is time of Elizabeth I. She inherited the throne from her catholic sister Mary, much to the chagrin of the English Catholics. They would much rather have had a Catholic Queen, and many set their eyes on Mary, Queen of Scots. <br/><br/>The main character of this book is Ned Willard. He is in love with Margery, but her parents have intended her for someone e</span>
  <span id="freeText3121589870084689767" style="display:none">I expect sumptuous historical novels from Ken Follett and he definitely delivered again. The cast of villains and heroes is vast. This time the setting is time of Elizabeth I. She inherited the throne from her catholic sister Mary, much to the chagrin of the English Catholics. They would much rather have had a Catholic Queen, and many set their eyes on Mary, Queen of Scots. <br /><br />The main character of this book is Ned Willard. He is in love with Margery, but her parents have intended her for someone else. Ned is drawn into the network around Elizabeth and becomes a spy, infiltrating the networks that would have her de-throned. Ned's enarmoured with Elizabeth from the beginning, and particularly into her relgious tolerance. Traitors must die though, and there are plenty of those.<br /><br />This is a truly sprawling historical novel, that delves deeply into polar opposites of Mary, Queen of Scots, and Elizabeth I. I learned quite a bit of history. I thought Mary Queen of Scots perhaps was Elizabeth's half sister or something - given that Henry VIII, her father, had such a lot of wives - but no, she was just a distant cousin. <br /><br />This was as deeply satisfying a novel as any by Ken Follett that I have read, despite the fact that it took me almost two weeks to read it. He is definitely one of my favorite authors in the historical fiction genre. Absolutely recommended!<br /><br />There is no need to worry about this being #3 in a series, it can be read as a stand alone without missing any serious points at all. Although the previous two do deserve to be read, there is no particular need to read read them in order, they are that far removed in time from each other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3121589870084689767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1805594851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1805594851" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15658501-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548681576p2/15658501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1805594851?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/15658501-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15658501-lindsey?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15658501-lindsey?shelf=tudor-england">tudor-england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15658501-lindsey?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15658501-lindsey?shelf=france">france</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805594851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11323904272684957556">I received a copy of the book from a Goodreads Giveaway.<br/><br/>I will start by saying I loved the first two books in the Kingsbridge series. I remember being engrossed with their stories so I was very excited to read the third installment. However, if you choose to write a Tudor-era book that is one of many in a sea of Elizabethan novels, it had better be fantastic and this just wasn't. It irritated me to no end that most of the fictional characters somehow took over the pivotal role in so many importa</span>
  <span id="freeText11323904272684957556" style="display:none">I received a copy of the book from a Goodreads Giveaway.<br /><br />I will start by saying I loved the first two books in the Kingsbridge series. I remember being engrossed with their stories so I was very excited to read the third installment. However, if you choose to write a Tudor-era book that is one of many in a sea of Elizabethan novels, it had better be fantastic and this just wasn't. It irritated me to no end that most of the fictional characters somehow took over the pivotal role in so many important events of that time-St Bartholomew's Day massacre, the Guy Fawkes gunpowder plot, Walsingham's spy ring, Mary Stuart's sole companion and solace (and no, Queen Mary did not have a close attendant named Alison-they were all named Mary), etc. It started to become comical, really, how important most of the characters made themselves to be in history. I would have enjoyed this story so much better if Follett had stuck to characters like Margery, Barney and Sylvie who embodied the spirit of the times without forcing themselves into prominence or if the real-life, true characters in the drama were fictionalized and allowed to tell their stories (like one of Queen Mary's Marys for example). I think I've been spoiled by my extensive reading of all things Tudor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11323904272684957556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2505206557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2505206557" />
    <a title="Ms.pegasus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5015851-ms-pegasus"><img alt="Ms.pegasus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335705124p2/5015851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2505206557?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms.pegasus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms.pegasus" href="/user/show/5015851-ms-pegasus">Ms.pegasus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ms.pegasus by: </span>
      selection of local book club
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015851-ms-pegasus?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015851-ms-pegasus?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2505206557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18144061725688463807">Great historical fiction immerses the reader in a different time and place. That state of immersion is shattered by glaring anachronisms. Some years ago I was watching a drama about Henry VIII. It included a dance scene that resembled a high school sock-hop more than a courtly diversion. That one scene ruined any possible sense of immersion. Writers beware: costumes and scenery alone are insufficient for creating historical fiction. <br/><br/>Unfortunately, I encountered the same problem with A COLUMN OF </span>
  <span id="freeText18144061725688463807" style="display:none">Great historical fiction immerses the reader in a different time and place. That state of immersion is shattered by glaring anachronisms. Some years ago I was watching a drama about Henry VIII. It included a dance scene that resembled a high school sock-hop more than a courtly diversion. That one scene ruined any possible sense of immersion. Writers beware: costumes and scenery alone are insufficient for creating historical fiction. <br /><br />Unfortunately, I encountered the same problem with A COLUMN OF FIRE, the third of Follett's historical trilogy that began in the middle ages. David Mitchell perceptively writes that an author of historical fiction must develop a personal “Bygonese.” Follett never tries for either the language or syntax that would evoke anything other than contemporary speech. The chatty narrative at least made this 900 page behemoth a quick read.<br /><br />Anachronisms abound in this book: “Girlie” (p.130) first known use 1857 (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/girlie);">https://www.merriam-webster.com/dicti...</a> “sexy” (p.134) first known use 1896 (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/sexy);">https://www.merriam-webster.com/dicti...</a> “grubby” (p.135) first known use 1725 (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/grubby">https://www.merriam-webster.com/dicti...</a>). It's a minor point but there are enough instances to cause the reader to forget that the speakers are of another time.<br /><br />The story follows the main character, Ned Willard, from 1558 to 1606. The period is filled with tumultuous events. It spans the reigns of three English monarchs and five French monarchs. (I was shocked to discover these years also spanned eight papacies. Fortunately, there's no hint of that in the book). The novel's scenes are set in England, Scotland, France, Spain and The Netherlands. More alarming, new characters kept bursting forth like the puppies in A HUNDRED AND ONE DALMATIANS. My advice is to note each character encountered in order to keep them all straight. This is particularly important for the intertwined royal and noble families of France.<br /><br />The book relies heavily on the reader's attachment to Ned. I never formed that strong attachment. I really didn't care about the Ned-Margery thread. I found the numerous secondary characters far more interesting. Ned's mother, Alice, is a shrewd merchant with interests in Calais and Seville. Ebrima is a slave working for Ned's cousin, Carlos. Both he and Carlos are forced to flee Spain. A second problem is that the characters lack dimension. Pierre and Rollo are both evil from the very beginning. <br /><br />What Follett excels at is devising suspenseful lead-ups into climactic scenes. A raid on Carlos' iron forge, numerous assassination plots, several harrowing escapes, and more than one murder keep the plot moving. Historic events like Queen Mary Stuart's execution and the St. Bartholomew's Day Massacre are mined with vivid prose. Between these episodes, however, were romantic threads that slowed the momentum of the book. Despite numerous historical details, I never felt like I was reading historical fiction.<br /><br />NOTES:<br />David Mitchell's astute essay on historical fiction:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/books/bookreviews/7685510/David-Mitchell-on-Historical-Fiction.html">https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/b...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18144061725688463807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13669334809366812201">Would have been better had it concentrated on the people of Kingsbridge. For me it turned into ‘just another’ book about Elizabeth and Mary. I enjoyed the first half but got bogged down in the second. It was a long book, but I needed more about the main characters and less about the wider world. In the early part of the book certain people were set up to be the main characters and then were hardly heard of again. I can’t help feeling that within the bones of this book, is a better one about King</span>
  <span id="freeText13669334809366812201" style="display:none">Would have been better had it concentrated on the people of Kingsbridge. For me it turned into ‘just another’ book about Elizabeth and Mary. I enjoyed the first half but got bogged down in the second. It was a long book, but I needed more about the main characters and less about the wider world. In the early part of the book certain people were set up to be the main characters and then were hardly heard of again. I can’t help feeling that within the bones of this book, is a better one about Kingsbridge.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorna" href="/user/show/6700518-lorna">Lorna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6700518-lorna?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2264688774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1017631034460265129"> <i>A Column of Fire</i> was the final book in the Kingsbridge trilogy taking place from 1558 through 1620 with history spanning some of the most turbulent and violent times including the Protestant Reformation, The Spanish Inquisition and the religious wars in France and England. This saga begins with the reign of Mary Tudor, Queen of England followed by her half-sister Elizabeth Tudor and the forty year imprisonment of Mary Queen of Scots. It also explores the struggles in France between the Catholic</span>
  <span id="freeText1017631034460265129" style="display:none"> <i>A Column of Fire</i> was the final book in the Kingsbridge trilogy taking place from 1558 through 1620 with history spanning some of the most turbulent and violent times including the Protestant Reformation, The Spanish Inquisition and the religious wars in France and England. This saga begins with the reign of Mary Tudor, Queen of England followed by her half-sister Elizabeth Tudor and the forty year imprisonment of Mary Queen of Scots. It also explores the struggles in France between the Catholics and the French Huguenots or French protestants with the massacre of St. Bartholomew's Day vividly portrayed.<br /><br /><i>". . . . the three great women of the sixteenth century were now dead: Elizabeth, Queen Caterina of France, and Margherita of Parma, governor of the Netherlands. They had all tried to stop men killing one another over religion. . . .Evil men had always frustrated the efforts of the peacemakers. Bloody religious wars had raged for decades in France and the Netherlands. Only England remained more or less at peace."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1017631034460265129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1229019-liviu?shelf=read_2017">read_2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060236967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15319818906346660023">a long book that moves extremely fast and while fairly predictable and with black and white characters without much subtlety, it is still very gripping and keeps one turning the pages; while technically Kingsbridge 3, the action is on a much larger canvas following the long religious struggle of the second half of the 16th century, mainly in England and France abut also in the Low Countries and even the Americas; a few notable events like the Night of st. Bartholomew in Paris, the long imprisonm</span>
  <span id="freeText15319818906346660023" style="display:none">a long book that moves extremely fast and while fairly predictable and with black and white characters without much subtlety, it is still very gripping and keeps one turning the pages; while technically Kingsbridge 3, the action is on a much larger canvas following the long religious struggle of the second half of the 16th century, mainly in England and France abut also in the Low Countries and even the Americas; a few notable events like the Night of st. Bartholomew in Paris, the long imprisonment, trial and execution of Mary Stuart, the defeat of the Armada and the Guy Fawkes plot are covered in detail but the narration moves effortlessly across years and forms a rounded whole with a great ending too; the usual Ken Follett prose (plain and no better or worse than in the Century trilogy) but the attractiveness of the novel is in its narrative energy and that it has in spades</span>
  <a data-text-id="15319818906346660023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6+OdPS3BroEXHlZw38aXtBsgelPpVWKr9W0hI1GswZx//l5zdEg45z56FVcimiKJnyFFo/Y3nKhNWNbXgM7wDg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pGTY+MyxZXEJuQE5Y+ECx6E+MriQaGRVMLhK7bq67/0weRu2lTjzFyDdQh6evbf6JT8NSI8KmlaIjb0Za9jebw==')})
  }

</script>

The novel Edge of Eternity narrates the fictional stories of the descendants of Ma Peshkov, their families and their associates in the United States, the United Kingdom, divided Germany and the USSR through the decades of the all-too-real existence of the Berlin Wall and the thrust of the United States Civil Rights movement and into the generation after. Several of them—notably George Jakes, Rebecca Held and Dimka Dvorkin—find themselves in positions of political power and influence near, but not at, the top of their countries’ governments across several decades. The ten-part narrative attends closely to them, as well as to their more artistically inclined cousins as they negotiate the sociopolitical turmoil of the 1960s, 1970s and 1980s, with a brief epilogue set in 2008.  Ken Follett’s sweeping Century Trilogy concludes with Edge of Eternity. It is a substantial read covering more than fifty years of recent history offering a detailed and authentic account of world events as they could have been seen by those in positions near those in power which will be looked at in this companion. As a work of historical fiction, it is based upon and treats real events, but it does so from the peripheries that, still closer to the action than many or most of the readers could be, lie outside those already so thoroughly known to history and almost mythologized in multiple retellings. Thus, Follett’s Edge of Eternity presents an unusual, and ultimately more compelling, perspective on the events that shaped the last third of the twentieth century and whose effects are still being felt a generation afterwards. Nevertheless, Edge of Eternity has its shortcomings. Kirsch, who was one of Langdon’s first students at Harvard two decades earlier, is about to reveal an astonishing breakthrough . . . one that will answer two of the fundamental questions of human existence. As the event begins, Langdon and several hundred guests find themselves captivated by an utterly original presentation, which Langdon realizes will be far more controversial than he ever imagined. But the meticulously orchestrated evening suddenly erupts into chaos, and Kirsch’s precious discovery teeters on the brink of being lost forever. Reeling and facing an imminent threat, Langdon is forced into a desperate bid to escape Bilbao. With him is Ambra Vidal, the elegant museum director who worked with Kirsch to stage the provocative event. Together they flee to Barcelona on a perilous quest to locate a cryptic password that will unlock Kirsch’s secret. Navigating the dark corridors of hidden history and extreme religion, Langdon and Vidal must evade a tormented enemy whose all-knowing power seems to emanate from Spain’s Royal Palace itself . . . and who will stop at nothing to silence Edmond Kirsch. On a trail marked by modern art and enigmatic symbols, Langdon and Vidal uncover clues that ultimately bring them face-to-face with Kirsch’s shocking discovery . . . and the breathtaking truth that has long eluded us.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3447.Ken_Follett">About Ken Follett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3447.Ken_Follett"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1604049089p3/3447.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3447.Ken_Follett">Ken Follett
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10533710877637644428">Ken Follett is one of the world’s most successful authors. Over 170 million copies of the 36 books he has written have been sold in over 80 countries and in 33 languages.<br/><br/>Born on June 5th, 1949 in Cardiff, Wales, the son of a tax inspector, Ken was educated at state schools and went on to graduate from University College, London, with an Honours degree in Philosophy – later to be made a Fellow of t</span>
  <span id="freeText10533710877637644428" style="display:none">Ken Follett is one of the world’s most successful authors. Over 170 million copies of the 36 books he has written have been sold in over 80 countries and in 33 languages.<br /><br />Born on June 5th, 1949 in Cardiff, Wales, the son of a tax inspector, Ken was educated at state schools and went on to graduate from University College, London, with an Honours degree in Philosophy – later to be made a Fellow of the College in 1995.<br /><br />He started his career as a reporter, first with his hometown newspaper the South Wales Echo and then with the London Evening News. Subsequently, he worked for a small London publishing house, Everest Books, eventually becoming Deputy Managing Director.<br /><br />Ken’s first major success came with the publication of Eye of the Needle in 1978. A World War II thriller set in England, this book earned him the 1979 Edgar Award for Best Novel from the Mystery Writers of America. It remains one of Ken’s most popular books.<br /><br />In 1989, Ken’s epic novel about the building of a medieval cathedral, The Pillars of the Earth, was published. It reached number one on best-seller lists everywhere and was turned into a major television series produced by Ridley Scott, which aired in 2010. World Without End, the sequel to The Pillars of the Earth, proved equally popular when it was published in 2007.<br /><br />Ken’s new book, The Evening and the Morning, will be published in September 2020. It is a prequel to The Pillars of the Earth and is set around the year 1,000, when Kingsbridge was an Anglo-Saxon settlement threatened by Viking invaders.<br /><br />Ken has been active in numerous literacy charities and was president of Dyslexia Action for ten years. He was chair of the National Year of Reading, a joint initiative between government and businesses. He is also active in many Stevenage charities and is President of the Stevenage Community Trust and Patron of Home-Start Hertfordshire.<br /><br />Ken, who loves music almost as much as he loves books, is an enthusiastic bass guitar player. He lives in Stevenage, Hertfordshire, with his wife Barbara, the former Labour Member of Parliament for Stevenage. Between them they have five children, six grandchildren and two Labradors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10533710877637644428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

But what makes The Pillars of the Earth extraordinary is the time the twelfth century; the place feudal England; and the subject the building of a glorious cathedral. Follett has re-created the crude, flamboyant England of the Middle Ages in every detail. The vast forests, the walled towns, the castles, and the monasteries become a familiar landscape. \n\nAgainst this richly imagined and intricately interwoven backdrop, filled with the ravages of war and the rhythms of daily life, the master storyteller draws the reader irresistibly into the intertwined lives of his characters into their dreams, their labors, and their loves: Tom, the master builder; Aliena, the ravishingly beautiful noblewoman; Philip, the prior of Kingsbridge; Jack, the artist in stone; and Ellen, the woman of the forest who casts a terrifying curse. From humble stonemason to imperious monarch, each character is brought vividly to life.\n\nThe building of the cathedral, with the almost eerie artistry of the unschooled stonemasons, is the center of the drama. Around the site of the construction, Follett weaves a story of betrayal, revenge, and love, which begins with the public hanging of an innocent man and ends with the humiliation of a king.\n\nFor the
